  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ac74e501-fa45-46b1-aea7-5f166877bb91'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/27816007-valerie-lussier"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1390081587i/27816007._UY100_CR39,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/27816007-valerie-lussier">Valerie Lussier</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Let's just say "'they" all dump Richard but he has some important parts along the way. Not sure which book you have read through. He was super whiney <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Let's just say "'they" all dump Richard but he has some important parts along the way. Not sure which book you have read through. He was super whiney at one point. Later on in the series it goes back and forward between wonderful books and some that I just tolerated. I loved Skin Trade. On the other hand, Cerulean Sins represents some time I will never get back. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1433879765" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1433879765" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1433879765?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-mystery">paranormal-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters">werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1433879765" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4528178408154463159">A dumb girl in love with both a vampire and a werewolf? This sounds slightly familiar...<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446719029i/16881886.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But, hey, this book was written first so I have a pretty good idea on who might have had the original idea.... (I'm smart like that.)<br/><br/>I liked this book slightly better than the last one. Anita is still pretty annoying, but I can still appreciate a few things about her.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>I crossed my arms on my stomach. A psychologist would have said I was closed off, uncommunicative. Fuck them.</i>
</b><br/><br/>See, I like that!<br/><br/>In this book, </span>
  <span id="freeText4528178408154463159" style="display:none">A dumb girl in love with both a vampire and a werewolf? This sounds slightly familiar...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446719029i/16881886.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, hey, this book was written first so I have a pretty good idea on who might have had the original idea.... (I'm smart like that.)<br><br>I liked this book slightly better than the last one. Anita is still pretty annoying, but I can still appreciate a few things about her.<br><br><b>
  <i>I crossed my arms on my stomach. A psychologist would have said I was closed off, uncommunicative. Fuck them.</i>
</b><br><br>See, I like that!<br><br>In this book, we have Anita trying to solve a case in which several shapeshifters have gone missing. She is also trying to figure out her relationship with Richard, a werewolf. Things get a little hairy with him.. (haha, hairy...see what I did there?) Strangely, for a girl who made a big statement about the fact that she won't date monsters, she is sure singing a different tune all of the sudden. I will go out on a limb here and say that humans dating animals is creepy. And, Richard definitely showed himself to be an animal in this book. His reaction to a very disturbing "snuff film" was equally disturbing.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446719029ra/16881887.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Hey, crabman!</i><br><br>But, for some reason, that doesn't scare Anita off. And, now she has agreed to date Jean Claude, the vampire king, at the same time as her wolf-man. That is one scary threesome. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446719029i/16881888.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Edward is becoming one of my favorite characters in this series. He is such a heartless mercenary, and yet he has a soft-spot for Anita. It cracked me up when he told Anita why he was following her:<br><br><b>
  <i>"Following you around lets me kill a lot of people."</i>
</b><br><br>That's very true, because as I have mentioned before, Anita has a big mouth and ends up having multiple attempts on her life in every book. Any bloodthirsty killer would love to follow her around and kill all of the people who are trying to kill her. He gets to look like a hero, all while fulfilling his murdery dreams. It's a win-win.<br><br>I hope Edward will keep showing up in the next books, but I have a feeling that there might be a point where he gets hired to kill Anita. I will actually be on Team Edward at that point.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446719029i/16881889.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="4528178408154463159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10789849311583232997">If I had to do this review in two words, it wouldn't be a challenge: Twilight Noir. Okay, it's historically inaccurate, since Stephenie Meyer stole the idea from Laurel K. Hamilton rather than vice versa, but apart from that it's close to the facts. We have the basic Twilight scenario: human woman is simultaneously in love with a vampire and a werewolf, but for bizarre reasons can't actually have sex with either of them. Instead of the infuriatingly wimpy Bella, though, we have tough-as-nails An</span>
  <span id="freeText10789849311583232997" style="display:none">If I had to do this review in two words, it wouldn't be a challenge: Twilight Noir. Okay, it's historically inaccurate, since Stephenie Meyer stole the idea from Laurel K. Hamilton rather than vice versa, but apart from that it's close to the facts. We have the basic Twilight scenario: human woman is simultaneously in love with a vampire and a werewolf, but for bizarre reasons can't actually have sex with either of them. Instead of the infuriatingly wimpy Bella, though, we have tough-as-nails Anita, who's your generic noir private eye. And instead of the bizarre Twilight plot we're served the usual noir routine, with Anita getting threatened, beaten up and shot at, as she wise-cracks her way from one perilous situation to another, kills the occasional supernatural creature or human, and, needless to say, solves the case. <br /><br /><b>The rest of this review is available elsewhere (the location cannot be given for Goodreads policy reasons)</b><br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=donated-gave-away">donated-gave-away</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63221671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4191999679481441041"><i>A Date-off?!?! Seriously?</i> Oh, what has become of you John Taylor...er, uh, Jean-Claude... <br/>Hamilton tries to introduce a love triangle. Tries. It ends up being a dating competition, and reminds me of a poorly written sitcom. Not what I would expect from a couple of super powerful, super sexy men. Anita was an even bigger disappointment, relationship wise. We learn that she is such a badass who doesn’t date because of a bad relationship. ONE bad relationship. Big deal. Who hasn’t had their heart b</span>
  <span id="freeText4191999679481441041" style="display:none"><i>A Date-off?!?! Seriously?</i> Oh, what has become of you John Taylor...er, uh, Jean-Claude... <br />Hamilton tries to introduce a love triangle. Tries. It ends up being a dating competition, and reminds me of a poorly written sitcom. Not what I would expect from a couple of super powerful, super sexy men. Anita was an even bigger disappointment, relationship wise. We learn that she is such a badass who doesn’t date because of a bad relationship. ONE bad relationship. Big deal. Who hasn’t had their heart broken? I also found it bizarre that Anita, Jean-Claude &amp; Richard seem to think that you can love someone (romantically) without actually liking them. Um… isn’t that just lust, then? At one point, Anita says of Richard that she doesn’t just love him, she actually likes him, too. Hmmm… Hamilton seems to have a pretty fucked up take on relationships. <br /><br />So far, this was my least favorite book of the series. I know this is a common complaint, but I could care less what color the Nike swoops are. It's curious that Hamilton pays such attention to detail over characters with horrible fashion sense. The majority of the outfits are all black anyway. And Jean-Claude...he just reeks of a white trash, wanna-be goth who doesn't dress as if he is very interested in attracting women. Black jeans with knee high velvet boots. White billowy shirt that is completely unbuttoned except for the ruby pendant at the collar. Is that attractive? No. No it is not. It's just bad taste. I keep imagining some acne afflicted kid at a renaissance fair. Yuck.<br /><br />Get back to the Zombie raising, Anita!<br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_341883249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/341883249" />
    <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light"><img alt="Crystal Starr Light" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573066911p2/3990525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/341883249?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crystal Starr Light" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crystal Starr Light" href="/user/show/3990525-crystal-starr-light">Crystal Starr Light</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143144045" href="/book/show/6411109-the-lunatic-cafe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=fashion-accident">fashion-accident</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=hello-my-name-is-mary-sue">hello-my-name-is-mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3990525-crystal-starr-light?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer341883249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer180509280740388074">Plot:<br/><br/>1) Client walks into Anita's office and asks her to do something. She refuses.<br/><br/>2) RELATIONSHIP DRAMA!<br/><br/>3) Dolph calls her to the scene of the crime.<br/><br/>4) Someone attacks Anita for no good reason.<br/><br/>5) The most disgusting crime scene EVAH!<br/><br/>6) MORE RELATIONSHIP DRAMA!<br/><br/>7) Oh, crap, there's a plot we're supposed to tie up. Okay, well, X does it.<br/><br/>8) Jean-Claude/Richard tries to get in Anita's pants. Anita makes stupid agreement.<br/><br/>9) BIG SHOWDOWN.<br/><br/>These books are getting formulaic. I guess if the formula were a</span>
  <span id="freeText180509280740388074" style="display:none">Plot:<br /><br />1) Client walks into Anita's office and asks her to do something. She refuses.<br /><br />2) RELATIONSHIP DRAMA!<br /><br />3) Dolph calls her to the scene of the crime.<br /><br />4) Someone attacks Anita for no good reason.<br /><br />5) The most disgusting crime scene EVAH!<br /><br />6) MORE RELATIONSHIP DRAMA!<br /><br />7) Oh, crap, there's a plot we're supposed to tie up. Okay, well, X does it.<br /><br />8) Jean-Claude/Richard tries to get in Anita's pants. Anita makes stupid agreement.<br /><br />9) BIG SHOWDOWN.<br /><br />These books are getting formulaic. I guess if the formula were a bit more interesting, I wouldn't mind so much. And in fact, towards the beginning of this book, I really liked it a lot. I actually was tempted to give it 4 stars and declare it my favorite so far.<br /><br />And then the RELATIONSHIP DRAMA began.<br /><br />Now, I understand why Anita is kinda iffy about Richard. He's a werewolf after all, and I too would be a bit hesitant before committing to a guy like that. But 1) she's considering committing after maybe two months of dating (she started dating him that October and this book is set in December!) and 2) she was wounded after a fiance dumped her. For point 1, I must ask, "Really?" I though Anita had a head on her shoulders, underneath that poufy, unmanageable hair. Why would she, even hastily, agree to marry Richard? Other than she refuses to have premarital sex because of her last relationship, and this woman SERIOUSLY needs to get laid.<br /><br />NOTE 1: I know that in a few books I am going to eat those words.<br /><br />NOTE 2: I have NO PROBLEMS with a person wanting to wait before having sex. That isn't the problem. The problem is...<br /><br />So Anita has sex with her fiance, and he dumps her. Yeah, that's rough, but we've all gone through relationship troubles. What makes her failed engagement TEH WORST EVAH? (Of course, maybe this is supposed to show her immaturity--she is only 24 after all...)<br /><br />Okay, let's say I buy all this relationship drama with Richard (and, for the most part, I do). What I do NOT understand is why Anita is so stupid to allow Jean-Claude, the dude she's been trying to foist off her for the last three books, suddenly force her into dating him. Anita, the guy is a creepy stalker dude. LET HIM BE. Don't date a guy like that!<br /><br />And that is what makes up a good 50% of the novel. About 10% is Anita getting into a p!ssing match with someone (because what book would be complete without Anita having to prove how awesome and adept she is?), and the rest is just action scene after action scene.<br /><br />The actual mystery is interesting. Disappearing shapeshifters? Looking into the werewolf subculture? Yeah, I'll buy that. But after awhile, I felt LKH was just tossing stuff at us to keep up the breakneck pace (the entire events of this book occur in less than a week). Werewolf snuff films, Anita killing a werewolf, Anita's relationship drama...all of this occurs so quickly, we barely have time to breath and think in between scenes. Even Anita is run ragged--that woman had better have the best damn health insurance, because by God, she goes to the hospital probably THREE TIMES in this book alone. And for God's sake, let the woman get a whole f@#$ing night of sleep, okay?<br /><br />And Anita? Ugh, how the hell does this unpleasant, unlikable, rude, arrogant woman get even ONE guy after her, much less TWO? It's absolutely ridiculous. If I were a man, I'd be running the other direction from her. I'm guessing that Jean-Claude and Richard are both extremely desperate to get laid. But even that isn't true--Jean-Claude has some German vampire chick after his marbled pecks, barely concealed by his god-awful frilly shirts.<br /><br />And you know what? I don't have to know what every gorram character is wearing in these books. I don't need to know if Anita is wearing a red sweater with an emerald green skirt and jacket and the jacket can't quite cover the Browning. I don't need an analysis of what knee-high black velvet boots Jean-Claude is using to complete his f@#$ing awful outfit. I don't care if Casper is wearing a tweed jacket or jeans or just his birthday suit. I don't need to know that Anita has changed out of those HORRIBLE heels (because REAL WOMEN can't wear those things!!) into her black Nikes to conceal all the blood and guts she gets in contact with. I DON'T CARE.<br /><br />What I DO care about is an interesting story. If you are going to go the route of Romantic Drama, don't bother with a mystery plot. But if you have a mystery plot, don't spend more of the book talking about how much of Jean-Claude's nipple we can see and whether or not Anita is going to marry Richard.<br /><br />On a brighter note (because this review suddenly became WAY more negative than I intended), I still like Ronnie and am even liking Dolph more. And I do like seeing all these other mythological creatures appear. And when they actually attempt to solve the mystery, it is pretty good. Oh, and I do think the action sequences are written pretty damn well.<br /><br />If I were a smart person, I'd probably stop here, but I do really want to see how the series progresses and if it gets better (before it gets worse). If you've read up to this book and have liked the ones before, I have no doubt you will probably like this one as well. But if the earlier books haven't sold you, it's doubtful this one is going to change your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="180509280740388074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction"><img alt="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605816027p2/2905339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93455205?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction" href="/user/show/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction">Bark  |  Ladies Of Horror Fiction</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2905339-bark-ladies-of-horror-fiction?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93455205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5045363605902210074">This book begins where the previous left off so your best bet is to read these in order so you can figure out how these tangled relationships develop into the mess that becomes Anita’s love life. Anita, Animator of the Dead, is seriously dating Richard the werewolf and is beginning to realize the perils of dating a “monster”. Jean Claude her other would-be beau is sticking his nose in their business because he’s a jealous little vampire-man and hasn’t been able to woo Anita with his vampire char</span>
  <span id="freeText5045363605902210074" style="display:none">This book begins where the previous left off so your best bet is to read these in order so you can figure out how these tangled relationships develop into the mess that becomes Anita’s love life. Anita, Animator of the Dead, is seriously dating Richard the werewolf and is beginning to realize the perils of dating a “monster”. Jean Claude her other would-be beau is sticking his nose in their business because he’s a jealous little vampire-man and hasn’t been able to woo Anita with his vampire charms and sea blue orbs of promised delight. I’m not a real big fan of the Jean Claude here. He does his best to ruin things for Richard and comes across as a bit of a mean-spirited brat. I was rooting for Richard in this book. His feelings seemed more real and I wanted him to have Anita, his teaching job and a peaceful normal life. If you hope for that too you may not want to read too much further along in this series. <br /><br />Anita is still raising zombies and helping out the spook squad but I noticed she begins to spend more time with the monsters and their politics here than in any of the previous books. She encounters evil vamp Gretchen as well as enters into the midst of the lycanthrope pack where she meets sadistic Marcus and Raina and sees first hand what the lycanthropes are capable of underneath all of the beauty. We also get more glimpses of hard-ass “I don’t bluff” Anita who refuses to back down from any big boy. It gets a little annoying in later books but here it still works, she’s still got shit to prove. Edward, AKA Death, plays a big role in this one and he’s always an enigmatic character who keeps my interest high. <br /><br />On the downside, we are once again inundated with endless boring descriptions of the hidden guns and the Nike swish color (mine is silver by the way in case you’re dying to know). Are you one of those freaks who will spend a sleepless night if you don’t have the most insignificant of details about Dolph’s wardrobe? Not to worry, here you go:<br /><br /><i>”His hands were plunged into pockets of a long black trench coat. The coat looked too thin for the weather but maybe it was lined, though he was a little bit too bulky to leave room for him and a lining in the same coat.”</i><br /><br />I don’t know about you but I wasn’t holding my breath wondering if Dolph wore a lined coat or not. Sheesh. Tell me something interesting and relevant to the story, like the fit of his undies or the secret spot he applies his cologne and I may finally stop complaining about these details.<br /><br />Seriously though, I like this book a whole bunch and think it is a solid entry in the series. Its old school Anita and her conflicted feelings about her two sexy men way back before she was uber powerful and attractive to every male in sight. Here she is still human with benefits just starting to make an appearance. She is vulnerable and I can relate to her need to be a tough girl. There are several subplots (but not enough to hurt my brain), lots of paranormal action and a whole lot of gore along with that slow burning sexual tension between the characters that I remember so well. I’m having a lot of fun revisiting this series and the imaginative world Laurell K. Hamilton built a decade or so ago. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5045363605902210074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228033036?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6289182-tilly-slaton?shelf=reviews-completed">reviews-completed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228033036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5080483562182837365">WARNING: This book is twisted and brilliant! Review contains certain details that are upsetting and some sexual reference is used. Thus .. the review will touch on a few details that are disgusting and unacceptable to sensitive and closed minds. If you are either of the above, please do not continue to read this review <br/><br/>I love this book! The Anita Blake series is AWESOME! Unfortunately, there are a few books in this series that just flat-out stink. The Lunatic Cafe is most definitely NOT one of t</span>
  <span id="freeText5080483562182837365" style="display:none">WARNING: This book is twisted and brilliant! Review contains certain details that are upsetting and some sexual reference is used. Thus .. the review will touch on a few details that are disgusting and unacceptable to sensitive and closed minds. If you are either of the above, please do not continue to read this review <br /><br />I love this book! The Anita Blake series is AWESOME! Unfortunately, there are a few books in this series that just flat-out stink. The Lunatic Cafe is most definitely NOT one of those books.<br /> <br />Filled with skinned and gutted victims, bestial pornographic snuff films, and forced romantic tangles, The Lunatic Cafe is by far one of the most interesting books in the Anita Blake series .. the first half of the series anyways.<br /> <br />I’ve always been a little twisted. Curiously intrigued by things that make others gag. What can I say? I’m a little weird. With that said, keep in mind when you read this book that although left intrigued and wondering .. that is not an implication of preference or justification of lifestyles by others. To each his own I just needed to explain this little bit to avoid confusion and concern by loved ones. <br /><br />I was so excited to read this book, that I completely forgot to highlight some fun parts for previewing pleasure. I did however, highlight a paragraph from one of the crime scenes. I think it’s totally rockin’ awesome. You may wrinkle your nose and find yourself disgusted. Woo hoo for individualism!<br /> <br /><i>Ragged furrows ran down the right side of his face. One claw had sliced over the eye, spilling blood and thick globs of eyeball down his cheek. The lower jaw was crushed, as if some great hand had grabbed it and squeezed. It made the face look unfinished, only half there. It must have hurt like hell, but it hadn’t killed him. More’s the pity.</i><br /> <br />The handsome Richard viewed as a monster? The sexy Jean-Claude grasping leverage to hostage intimate moments from Anita? <br /> <br />A sexual-sadist, Raina, an alpha werewolf to the local pack and Richard’s former lover, climbs under Blake’s skin and wiggles around, leaving Blake disgusted with the idea that Richard could ever be involved with such a monster.<br /> <br />Nasty, manipulative witches. Nagas seeking rescue. Shapeshifters missing. This book has a wide range of plots that continually catch you off guard. Just when you think you’ve figured it all out, you’re blindsided by something entirely unexpected and delicious.<br /> <br />I recommend this book to curious minds, those pushing lines of moral reality, and those with their feet firmly planted on the ground. There is more to a normal life, and this book covers several aspects of life that are shunned and ignored by a society of manners and a certain set of acceptable sexual standards.<br /> <br />ADULTS ONLY! I highly recommend you store this book away from curious little hands. Although open-minded, I strenuously object to younger minds reading this book. And even so .. here on out .. ANY book from this series.<br /> <br />Filled with beautifully crafted and blood dripping crime scenes, obscenely provocative and perverted sexual content .. The Lunatic Cafe will leave you wondering just how far other people will go to satisfy their needs and desires!<br /> <br /><i>“There are more roads to monsterdom than most people realize.”</i><br /> <br />Woo hoo! HAPPY READING!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5080483562182837365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText16550807873661750682" style="display:none">With each book in this series, Anita Blake is really growing on me as a character. <br />I’m finding that I’m enjoying each instalment more and more as I’m progressing through the series.<br /><br />Set after the events of the previous novel, Anita is asked to investigate a series of shapeshifter disappearances.<br /><br />The main focus of the novel delves into Anita’s personal life with werewolf boyfriend Richard and the continued advances of vampire Jean-Claude...<br /><br />A Werewolf/Vampire love triangle instantly draws parallels to Twilight.<br />But with this book initially published during the mid-90’s and Anita’s kickass attitude, the storyline still feels fresh and interesting 20 years later.<br /><br />The mystery itself was interesting and helped keep up the pace.<br />Hamilton perfectly blends the romance and action perfectly.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85773361?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/3084363-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3084363-sabrina?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer85773361&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85773361" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer810403481289844338">It's a bit sad how Hamilton has some decent storylines, but manages to deliver them so poorly and secondary that the main point of this novel is a date-off between Jean-Claude and Richard. It doesn't really get any more superfluous than this - I hope! Considering there are still 13 more books to this series, I fear it probably will. <br/><br/>Anita went from "ok, she is not Buffy, but at least she's a bit kickass" to being just an ass. She's completely self-righteous and probably the biggest monster of th</span>
  <span id="freeText810403481289844338" style="display:none">It's a bit sad how Hamilton has some decent storylines, but manages to deliver them so poorly and secondary that the main point of this novel is a date-off between Jean-Claude and Richard. It doesn't really get any more superfluous than this - I hope! Considering there are still 13 more books to this series, I fear it probably will. <br /><br />Anita went from "ok, she is not Buffy, but at least she's a bit kickass" to being just an ass. She's completely self-righteous and probably the biggest monster of them all. Whenever she goes around killing people, it's alright and no big deal, but everyone else just can't live up to her standards - which she makes up as she goes. Jean-Claude must have really had some horrible centuries if Anita Blake is his ideal woman.<br /><br />The storywriting made me cringe - this is only the fourth book and there are already so many passages, phrases and character descriptions which are copied and pasted from the first one. I understand that you can have a few catch phrases which are repeated througout the series, but some passages about places (Anita's apartment, Jean-Claude's office..) are just 1:1 copied. Aswell as descriptions and characterisations of people which either show Hamilton's lack of writing skills or lack or interesting characters. <br />Descriptions of clothes and the not really interesting love triangle get more paragraphs than the actual story - which is really sad even for chick lit. The story and the twist is again not bad, but it's overshadowed by completely irrelevant babble. </span>
  <a data-text-id="810403481289844338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1620264619" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1620264619" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10094360-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411487938p2/10094360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1620264619?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/10094360-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/7797366-the-lunatic-cafe">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1620264619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4226585442407365145">WHYYYY are these books so bad? They have potential. A lot of potential. But instead of focusing on what is absolutely necessary in a 25+ book series, namely, character development and world-building, Hamilton focuses on action scenes and a whole bunch of stupid, pointless plot that keeps the story moving but gives us nothing.<br/><br/>I finished this book less than 48 hours ago and I can hardly remember anything that happened. There were a bunch of shapeshifter action scenes, lots of Anita just being a st</span>
  <span id="freeText4226585442407365145" style="display:none">WHYYYY are these books so bad? They have potential. A lot of potential. But instead of focusing on what is absolutely necessary in a 25+ book series, namely, character development and world-building, Hamilton focuses on action scenes and a whole bunch of stupid, pointless plot that keeps the story moving but gives us nothing.<br /><br />I finished this book less than 48 hours ago and I can hardly remember anything that happened. There were a bunch of shapeshifter action scenes, lots of Anita just being a straight up bitch, and what is potentially the dumbest love triangle I have ever read. Dude, the love triangle in Twilight made more sense than this one. Anita claims she loves the vampire...Um, HOW? You literally hate everything about him, everything he does, everything he says. Thinking he's hot does not make you love him. And the whole agreeing-to-date-vampire-while-werewolf-stands-by-before-she-makes-a-decision thing is insane. Do grown people do this? Wtf???? And accepting a proposal while you're half naked getting hot and heavy? Again, wtfffffff.<br /><br />This series can be redeemed. I want backstory -- why is Anita so rude and condescending? What made her this way? Why is Richard such a sap? Why is Edward obsessed with killing like, everything? I understand Jean-Claude. I don't get anyone else. None of their actions make sense to me. <br /><br />Also, let me understand the world! Every book there is quick mention of new creatures, new groups and beliefs and laws, but nothing is expanded upon. This world is seriously intriguing (no sarcasm). So give me more world-building and less descriptions of Anita's hideous outfits for crying out loud!<br /><br />In conclusion, here are some things Anita needs to STFU about:<br /><br />The color of the swish on her Nikes. NO ONE CARES.<br />Descriptions of her ~ironic~ Christmas sweaters. You're not cute.<br />Her pretentious coffee. Especially when she made a cup that she claimed would "grow hair on someone's chest" and it was VANILLA FLAVORED. Hahahaha seriously? I've been taking it black since I was 16. Your vanilla coffee ain't shit.<br />Her stupid penguin collection.<br />Guns and holsters and knives. Obviously.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4226585442407365145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16942435934136607605">What a treat, to find out you have a cousin who shares your reading habits! My public library has this book on order and I’ve been waiting for it for <u>months</u>! While visiting over New Year’s, my cousin & I got discussing this series, and she sent me home with a suitcase full of reading material—a happy New Year indeed.<br/><br/>Although some aspects of the series are silly, I’m enjoying it despite that. I mean Anita accepts a marriage proposal from a man (well, a werewolf) she really barely knows—and that b</span>
  <span id="freeText16942435934136607605" style="display:none">What a treat, to find out you have a cousin who shares your reading habits! My public library has this book on order and I’ve been waiting for it for <u>months</u>! While visiting over New Year’s, my cousin &amp; I got discussing this series, and she sent me home with a suitcase full of reading material—a happy New Year indeed.<br /><br />Although some aspects of the series are silly, I’m enjoying it despite that. I mean Anita accepts a marriage proposal from a man (well, a werewolf) she really barely knows—and that becomes more and more obvious as the book progresses—and even though she has serious misgivings, they keep on as if they were actually going to go through with a wedding. Then her vampiric nemesis, Jean-Claude objects, stating that if she has feelings for him too, he should get equal time to press his suit. <i>And Anita takes this bit of sophistry seriously.</i> I mean, last time I checked, women were allowed to marry as they chose and didn’t have to give anybody equal time to make an impression! (Besides, I’m usually of the opinion that if a woman really does have feelings for two men, she shouldn’t have to make a decision between them!)<br /><br />I will also confess to a bout of severe eye-rolling when I read Anita’s reasons for not sleeping with either of them. Betrayed by her first fiancée? OMG. But, as a plot device to keep the love triangle stretched out, it works beautifully. Will I continue to read? Of course! Especially since I now have a suitcase full of Anita Blake books to keep me supplied.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16942435934136607605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8352106335461352901" style="display:none">So I just finished it. I have to say I've started to not like Anita already. <div id="review_149848615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149848615" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4825603-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1309958279p2/4825603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149848615?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/4825603-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4825603-amanda?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149848615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13526289921306493644">I keep reading these books and the further I get, the more I just struggle to continue. This series was highly recommended from some friends. I thought, what the heck and started reading. The story lines are OK, the love interest are alright, but the characters drive me batty. They make it really hard for me to connect and engage in the story. <br/><br/>Anita is this tough as nails chick who doesn't like help, ask for help, or respect you if you offer her help. She is hard core all the way. I get what the</span>
  <span id="freeText13526289921306493644" style="display:none">I keep reading these books and the further I get, the more I just struggle to continue. This series was highly recommended from some friends. I thought, what the heck and started reading. The story lines are OK, the love interest are alright, but the characters drive me batty. They make it really hard for me to connect and engage in the story. <br /><br />Anita is this tough as nails chick who doesn't like help, ask for help, or respect you if you offer her help. She is hard core all the way. I get what the writer is trying to do with this character, but it isn't working. You can be an independent tough chick and still have a soft side. There is no soft side with Anita and she is, in my opinion, cruel to her supposed love interest Richard. The other thing I cannot stand is that she keeps saying she is out to protect the innocent and she is "good". I don't get that with her. I don't get that she is "good" or doing this stuff for the right reasons. <br /><br />Jean Claude (up to this book, I've heard rumors that you start to see a different prespective in the next) is hard core vampire who isn't afraid to torture anybody so that he can remain in charge of his city as Master. Part of me wants to like him, but I struggle with it. I haven't pinpointed why and maybe if I decide to continue the series my opinion will change.<br /><br />Richard is a good werewolf who doesn't believe in killing just to kill. It is an interesting character and I actually like him. He's a good guy who does things for the right reason. Honestly, he is way to good for Anita and I wish he would walk and find himself a sweet girl who does love him, disease and all.<br /><br />The storyline in this book is OK. It is more of bad guys threatening the bad Anita who sleeps with her guns and gets into situations with a lot of blood. I think these books are supposed to be crime mysterious with supernatural thrown in. This book had a good mystery in it when the writer actually focused on it and not just on putting Anita into situations where she was going to end up bloody. I can't decide if it is time for me to step away from this series or continue to see if there is any redemption left. Decisions, decisions. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13526289921306493644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1528195823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528195823" />
    <a title="Alen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10259320-alen"><img alt="Alen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586344821p2/10259320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528195823?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alen" href="/user/show/10259320-alen">Alen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10259320-alen?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10259320-alen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10259320-alen?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10259320-alen?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10259320-alen?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10259320-alen?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528195823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6999933054703744525"><b>DO NOT READ THIS IF YOU DON'T WANT TO READ ANY SPOILERS </b><br/><br/>Anita Blake has got a hot date, with Richard, the werewolf she's been dating for a few months only. As she describes, they're still not very intimate, since they barely know each other. But as you know, if you've read this book, their relationship just goes really fast, way too fast in my opinion. <br/><br/>Jean-Claude is still trying to interfere with their relationship, for some reason. At this point I think this love-triangle, (turned into love-sq</span>
  <span id="freeText6999933054703744525" style="display:none"><b>DO NOT READ THIS IF YOU DON'T WANT TO READ ANY SPOILERS </b><br><br>Anita Blake has got a hot date, with Richard, the werewolf she's been dating for a few months only. As she describes, they're still not very intimate, since they barely know each other. But as you know, if you've read this book, their relationship just goes really fast, way too fast in my opinion. <br><br>Jean-Claude is still trying to interfere with their relationship, for some reason. At this point I think this love-triangle, (turned into love-square) is just getting more and more stupid. I really wasn't able to see the point. But still, you'll see Anita admitting she loves both JC and Richard, even if in different ways -wtf?- Anita, get your act together, you don't know either men well enough to say that. As a matter in fact, you sure don't know Richard to accept his marriage proposal just because you want to jump his bones. Yes people, although Anita feels no remorse when she's got to kill someone or something, she feels remorse about having pre-marital sex. - Bitch, get your priorities straight!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380345610ra/700243.gif" width="500" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for the crime that takes place this time, or crimes, we got a disappearance, a female shapeshifter<br>has gone missing for a few days, Anita delivers this case to Ronnie, her bff, because that's just not what her job is about. There's also a brutal murder (as usual), a man is found in the snow half-eaten by a bear (or is it?). Marcus, an alpha werewolf, who also happens to want to kill Richard, calls Anita to go to the Lunatic Cafe to have a few words with him. We all know that something else goes on besides those said words. <br><br>Although Anita Blake still manages to be one of the most badass female characters I've ever had the pleasure to meet, I gotta ask: Why the f*** does she wear corny-ass clothing? Everything about her sense of fashion is simply wrong! And I'm not a fashion guru, I'm more of a tshirt-and-jeans kind of gall. Why doesn't she just dress herself like the typical UF badass heroine? Leather black pants, leather black jacket, Doc Martens and a sexy top? I got nothing against that. Instead Anita is a fan of fanny packs... That's just wrong in so many levels.<br><br>That's why folks, the first thing I advise you to do while reading an Anita Blake book is to completely ignore her outfit. Just picture what you would like to see her wearing. I sure as heck do that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455677871ra/18135261.gif" width="450" height="279" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Speaking of clothing, since I'm sounding like Fashion Police, let's talk about Jean-Claude's cape, yay or nay? I kinda like it, I think it's ridiculous, but it just suits him.<br><br><br>Let's take a look at the people I hated on this book:<br>-Aikensen<br>-Titus<br>-Raina<br>-Markus - he's such an idiot, seriously! How can anybody follow his orders? That scene with Alfred was just full-on crazy stupid. <br>-Kaspar -what even!! A wereswan whose name is Kaspar, can you think of something more hilarious? No? What about Anita's fanny pack? That gets the prize.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385177889ra/7089410.gif" width="245" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The people I loved on this book:<br>-Edward - not surprisingly, I just love Edward way too much. Anita should bet on this guy, even if he is kind of psychopatish... Oh Edward *sighs*<br>-Gabriel??? I'm not sure, this dude likes pain way too much, but he just seems really hot. - yes, I'm just that superficial. I hope we see more of him in the future.<br><br>Then there's also Anita's mug collection, now I'd love to see a whole video haul on that, she has really funny mugs she likes to take to the office just to annoy the hell out of Bert, her boss. I find that highly entertaining, just like her stuffed penguin collection. A girl's got to have muscle on her, but a girl's also got to have someone to hold on to, even if it's a stuffed animal, I'm all for that. (I love my stuffed alpaca, which I hold all night long). <br><br>As for fav quotes:<br><i>I had to smile. I knew more monsters than the monsters did.</i><br><br><i>"Following you around let's me kill a lot of people." Sad but true.</i> - I don't believe I have said it enough times: I LOVE EDWARD.<br><br><i>Sometime in February a box arrived from Edward. It was a swan skin. The note read, "I found a witch to lift his curse".</i> - OH EDWARD I SAW WHAT YOU DID THERE, HAHAHA<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6999933054703744525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2734564490976316077">I freely admit that I have problems with Hamilton's writing. You see, she has a great gift for tense plotting and engaging writing. But instead of utilizing her talents, she turns her books into ridiculous will-they-won't-they soaps. Basically, this book was all about Anita facing off Jean-Claude on the one hand and mulling over Richard on the other. And the back and forth of that quickly became more than annoying. The plot itself - the search for the killer - took what? 60 pages? Everything els</span>
  <span id="freeText2734564490976316077" style="display:none">I freely admit that I have problems with Hamilton's writing. You see, she has a great gift for tense plotting and engaging writing. But instead of utilizing her talents, she turns her books into ridiculous will-they-won't-they soaps. Basically, this book was all about Anita facing off Jean-Claude on the one hand and mulling over Richard on the other. And the back and forth of that quickly became more than annoying. The plot itself - the search for the killer - took what? 60 pages? Everything else was shipping or gratuitous gore. Anita being all obnoxious and uppity, especially towards Richard, was... Ugh. I can understand her misgivings. But not her hypocrisy.<br /><br />Well, I will probably read the next book in the series but for once I'm glad that I'm simply borrowing these books and not owning them - I'm quite sure that I won't be doing any actual re-reads.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_87928121" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87928121" />
    <a title="Dichotomy Girl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2462318-dichotomy-girl"><img alt="Dichotomy Girl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443544131p2/2462318.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87928121?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dichotomy Girl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dichotomy Girl" href="/user/show/2462318-dichotomy-girl">Dichotomy Girl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2462318-dichotomy-girl?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2462318-dichotomy-girl?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2462318-dichotomy-girl?shelf=paranormal-or-spec">paranormal-or-spec</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87928121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18419551527454197813">2018 Reread to figure out where this series went so horribly wrong:<br/><br/>And it begins. At the halfway point of this book Anita makes two decisions that sent her course for the future.<br/><br/>#1. She says yes to Richard's proposal, even though they is constant friction because Richard wants a soft gentle woman to protect and make him feel human, and Anita wants someone human who accepts that she is tough and prone to violence. She also is uncomfortable with Richard in her apartment, and irritated that her FIA</span>
  <span id="freeText18419551527454197813" style="display:none">2018 Reread to figure out where this series went so horribly wrong:<br /><br />And it begins. At the halfway point of this book Anita makes two decisions that sent her course for the future.<br /><br />#1. She says yes to Richard's proposal, even though they is constant friction because Richard wants a soft gentle woman to protect and make him feel human, and Anita wants someone human who accepts that she is tough and prone to violence. She also is uncomfortable with Richard in her apartment, and irritated that her FIANCE cooked her dinner.<br /><br />#2. She doesn't take the out that Richard offers her after she clearly finds out that Richard is as unhuman as Jean-Claude.<br /><br />#3. She lets Jean-Claude manipulate her into agreeing to date him. She reasons that if she is Ok with Richard not being human, then she must also date Jean-Claude. FALSE! It has been laid out numerous time in the previous #3 books that Anita is a Christian, that she believes vampires to be be: dead, soulless, and basically evil (bound for hell and all that). It has also been established that lycanthropes are HUMANS who have been infected by a disease, which changes them genetically, but not necessarily spiritually.<br /><br />However, she seems to completely forget this in this book, effectively saying instead "Hey, if I'll date one non-human than I'll date all of them."<br /><br />This is her first step to becoming one of the monsters. And honestly, if Laurell K. Hamilton had been a really good author. She could have used this. As Anita gets pulled further and further away from her principles, until the day that she wakes up and realizes that she has become that which she hates....THAT is where the series should have ended, and it would have been Awesome.<br /><br />(That's my Head Cannon anyway.....)<br /><br />To be Continued...<br /><br />In the afterward of the re-release of this book, the author states that she realizes now that this was the beginning of the end for Anita and Richard. Which is ironic, as their entire relationship prior to this book was off screen. (In the last book they are having their first date, in this book they are engaged). I honestly can't see how Anita and Richard would have gotten past those first few dates. They are so incompatible that it's laughable....and this before Anita turns into a supernatural whore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18419551527454197813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10382116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2502935702552648957">I'm always in search of a good vampire story, so I read the first four Anita Blake books. I think Laurell K. Hamilton had a potentially interesting concept creating a world where most supernatural elements are real and integrated into society. I like the concept of were-(insert any animal here). What I don't like about Anita Blake books is Anita Blake! It's hard to read books when the protagonist has an abrasive personality and nothing witty to say. You can look forward to Anita's verbal confron</span>
  <span id="freeText2502935702552648957" style="display:none">I'm always in search of a good vampire story, so I read the first four Anita Blake books. I think Laurell K. Hamilton had a potentially interesting concept creating a world where most supernatural elements are real and integrated into society. I like the concept of were-(insert any animal here). What I don't like about Anita Blake books is Anita Blake! It's hard to read books when the protagonist has an abrasive personality and nothing witty to say. You can look forward to Anita's verbal confrontations with an authority figure or tall blonde female at least once every few chapters, and a page-long description of her outfit every time she goes to a new location. <br /><br />ps- I realize I'm probably not the target audience for these books. But I feel sorry for poor Richard. Anita treats him like a CHUMP. Dump her!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2502935702552648957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42743525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18009029093679213119">I think this was my favorite so far. Or maybe they are just getting better because I read them in order. I would like to see Anita give in to Richard a little but she really never does and that is a major part of her character, keeping her focus. Edward makes an appearance in every book so I wonder if anything romantic will happen between the two. Anita is always complaining that the men in her life perusing her are all monsters so what gives. </span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5K0Oyh+JIkEVztmwFTVpok64hw1RfqMJeZYfPxBikRnivHP+t/uAmmJLt3VHpijc3b453H4AHh9wLQtdZShZOw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZgEPhCzIy9OM4b0wSmgUE58HYRNY9IBV2Io2zUQenA5gEHKwhLppCPtk0/UY+1VtDAHfwneKPUPRMSKvMVRULA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8918316494726115590">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis </span>
  <span id="freeText8918316494726115590" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>

The investigation leads her to Cerulean Sins, a vampire-run establishment that deals in erotic videos, videos that cater to very specific tastes. Anita knows one creature of the night who has such interests — Jean-Claude’s visitor. But if Anita brings Musette down, the repercussions could cost her everything she holds dear.\n\nOnce a sworn enemy of all monsters, Anita is now the human consort of both Master Vampire Jean Claude and leopard shapeshifter Micah. When a centuries-old vampire hits St. Louis, Anita finds herself needing all the dark forces her passion can muster to save the ones she loves.\n\nAnita Blake returns to find hell hath no fury like a
